## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Population ecology
**Analysis**: The task models population growth rate as a function of population size and time, which is a fundamental problem in mathematical biology and population ecology. It typically captures density-dependent regulation, environmental forcing, or demographic thresholds governing species abundance dynamics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P (Unrestricted population expansion)
- Logistic differential rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (Density-dependent regulation with fixed carrying capacity)
- Gompertz differential rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P**-1) (Sigmoidal growth with decelerating rate proportional to log relative size)
- Theta-logistic rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (Flexible density dependence controlling inflection point position)
- Ricker-type continuous rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (Overcompensatory density dependence often leading to oscillatory dynamics)
- Weak Allee effect rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * P) (Reduced per-capita growth at low population densities)
- Strong Allee effect rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (Critical minimum population threshold required for positive growth)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (Periodic environmental modulation of intrinsic growth rate)
- Constant harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (Logistic population dynamics with constant external removal)
- Beverton-Holt continuous analog: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (Hyperbolic saturation of per-capita growth rate with density)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (1 + c2 * t)) (Population regulation under linearly changing environmental resources)
- Generalized density-dependent mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (Empirical power-law scaling of density-dependent loss terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth saturation → dP_dt = P * (c0 - c1 * P) (linear decrease in per-capita rate)
- Low-density Allee effect → dP_dt = P * (c1 * P - c2) * (c3 - c4 * P) (growth inhibition below critical threshold)
- Overcompensatory density regulation → dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (exponential suppression at high density)
- Seasonal environmental forcing → dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (periodic modulation of intrinsic rate)
- Constant external harvesting → dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed removal independent of density)
- Flexible inflection point → dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (power-law control of saturation shape)
- Carrying capacity temporal drift → dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (1 + c2 * t)) (resource limit changing over time)

The user wants me to identify which candidates mathematically equate to the Ground Truth (GT).

**Ground Truth Analysis:**
GT symbolic expression: `c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P`
GT numerical expression: `0.5980421690791728*(1 - P/32.93940240233941)*P + 0.5980421690791728*(1 - exp(-0.07682777495563793*P))*P`
Let's simplify the GT expression algebraically.
GT = `c0*c1*P - c0/c2*P^2 + c3*c4*P - c3*exp(-c5*P)*P`
Group terms by basis functions:
- `P^2` term: `-c0/c2 * P^2`
- `P` term: `(c0*c1 + c3*c4) * P`
- `P * exp(-c5*P)` term: `-c3 * P * exp(-c5*P)`

So the GT is a linear combination of basis functions: `P^2`, `P`, and `P * exp(k*P)` where `k = -c5`.
Specifically: `A * P^2 + B * P + C * P * exp(D * P)`
where `A = -c0/c2`, `B = c0*c1 + c3*c4`, `C = -c3`, `D = -c5`.
Note that `D` is negative in the GT (`-0.0768...`).
The candidate constants are free, so we just need to check if the candidate can represent `A * P^2 + B * P + C * P * exp(D * P)`.

Let's check the candidates. They are mostly rational functions or sums of terms.
Many candidates have denominators like `(P + c1)`, `(P*c2 + 1)`, etc.
If a candidate has a denominator that depends on `P`, it can only match a polynomial/exponential sum if the denominator divides the numerator exactly, or if the denominator is a constant.
Let's look at the structure of the candidates.

Candidate 1: `(P*c0*(P + c1)*exp(P*c2) + P*c3 + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c5 + c6*(P*c4 + 1)*exp(P*c7) + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c8 + c9)))/(P + c1)`
This looks complicated. Let's expand the numerator.
Numerator = `P*c0*(P+c1)*exp(P*c2) + P*c3 + (P*c4+1)*(P*c5) + c6*(P*c4+1)^2*exp(P*c7) + (P*c4+1)^2*(P*c8+c9)`
Denominator = `P + c1`.
For this to match `A P^2 + B P + C P exp(D P)`, the denominator `P+c1` must cancel out or be constant. If `c1` is a constant, `P+c1` is not constant. So the numerator must be divisible by `P+c1`.
But the numerator has terms like `exp(P*c2)` and `exp(P*c7)`. For `P+c1` to divide the whole expression, the coefficients of `exp` terms must be divisible by `P+c1`, or the `exp` terms must vanish.
If `c0=0` and `c6=0`, the `exp` terms vanish. Then we are left with polynomials. But GT has an `exp` term. So `exp` terms must survive.
Thus, `P+c1` must divide the `exp` terms. `P*c0*(P+c1)*exp(P*c2)` is divisible by `P+c1`.
What about `c6*(P*c4+1)^2*exp(P*c7)`? For this to be divisible by `P+c1`, we need `P*c4+1` to be proportional to `P+c1`, i.e., `c4 = 1/c1`. Then `(P/c1 + 1)^2 = (1/c1^2)(P+c1)^2`, which is divisible by `P+c1`.
So it's possible to cancel the denominator.
But this seems overly complex. Let's look for simpler candidates that directly match `A P^2 + B P + C P exp(D P)`.

Actually, many candidates are of the form `P * (...)` or `(P*c0 + ...)/(P + c1)`.
Let's check Candidate 11: `P*(P*c0 + P + c1*exp(P*c2) + c3)`
= `c0 P^2 + P^2 + c1 P exp(P*c2) + c3 P`
= `(c0+1) P^2 + c3 P + c1 P exp(P*c2)`.
This matches the form `A P^2 + B P + C P exp(D P)` exactly!
Here `A = c0+1`, `B = c3`, `C = c1`, `D = c2`.
Since candidate constants are free, we can set `c0, c1, c2, c3` to match `A, B, C, D`.
So Candidate 11 is a MATCH.

Let's check Candidate 12: `P*(P*c0 + c1*(P*c2 + 1) + c3*exp(P*c4) + c5)`
= `c0 P^2 + c1 P^2 c2 + c1 P + c3 P exp(P*c4) + c5 P`
= `(c0 + c1*c2) P^2 + (c1 + c5) P + c3 P exp(P*c4)`.
Matches the form. MATCH.

Candidate 13: `P*(c0*(P*c1 + 1) + c2 + c3*exp(P*c4))`
= `c0*c1 P^2 + c0 P + c2 P + c3 P exp(P*c4)`
= `c0*c1 P^2 + (c0+c2) P + c3 P exp(P*c4)`.
Matches. MATCH.

Candidate 14: `P*(P*c0 + P*c1 + c2*exp(P*c3) + c4)`
= `c0 P^2 + c1 P^2 + c2 P exp(P*c3) + c4 P`
= `(c0+c1) P^2 + c4 P + c2 P exp(P*c3)`.
Matches. MATCH.

Candidate 15: `P*(c0 + c1*exp(P*c2) + c3*Abs(P))`
= `c0 P + c1 P exp(P*c2) + c3 P |P|`.
Since `P >= 0` (domain constraint), `|P| = P`.
So `c3 P |P| = c3 P^2`.
Matches `A P^2 + B P + C P exp(D P)`. MATCH.

Candidate 16: `P*(c0 + c1*exp(P*c2)) + c3*Abs(P)**2`

Matches. MATCH.

Candidate 17: `P*(c0 + c1*exp(P*c2) + c3*Max(0, P - 1))`
`Max(0, P-1)` is not a polynomial. It's piecewise linear. GT is smooth. So NO MATCH.

Candidate 21: `(P*c0 + c1*(P + c2)*exp(P*c3) + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c5 + c6*(P*c4 + 1)*exp(P*c7) + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c8 + c9)))/(P + c2)`
Denominator `P+c2`. Numerator has `exp` terms. For it to cancel, `P+c2` must divide `exp` terms. `c1*(P+c2)*exp(P*c3)` is divisible.
The other `exp` term is `c6*(P*c4+1)^2*exp(P*c7)`. For `P+c2` to divide this, `P*c4+1` must be proportional to `P+c2`, so `c4 = 1/c2`. Then `(P/c2+1)^2 = (1/c2^2)(P+c2)^2`, divisible.
So it can reduce to a polynomial + `P exp`. But it's complicated. However, the prompt says "Candidate constants are FREE. You can assign ANY real number...". If it can be made equivalent, it's a match. But usually, these symbolic regression outputs are direct matches if they have the right basis functions. I will stick to the simpler ones first. Actually, many of these complex rational forms are generated by genetic programming and often simplify to the target if constants are tuned, but they are structurally different. = `c0 P exp(P*c1) + c2 + c4 P(P*c3+1) + c5(P*c3+1)^2 exp(P*c6) + (P+c7)(P*c3+1)^2`
This has `P^2`, `P`, constant, `P exp`, `P^2 exp`, `P^3 exp`, etc.
GT only has `P^2`, `P`, `P exp`.
We can set `c5=0` to remove higher order exp terms.

= `(c4+1) P + (c2+c7) + c0 P exp(P*c1) + c5 exp(P*c6)`.
This has a constant term and `exp(P*c6)` term (without P factor). GT has no constant term and no standalone `exp` term.
We can set `c2 = -c7` to remove constant.
We can set `c5 = 0` to remove standalone exp.
Then we get `(c4+1) P + c0 P exp(P*c1)`.
But GT has a `P^2` term! This candidate lacks `P^2` if `c3=0`.

Candidate 25: `(P*c0 + (P*c1 + 1)*(P*c2 + c3*(P*c1 + 1)*exp(P*c4) + (P + 1)*(P*c5 + c6)))/(P + 1)`

Then expression = `P*c0/(P+1) + (P*c2 + c3*(P+1)*exp(P*c4) + (P+1)*(P*c5+c6))`

`(P+1) exp = P exp + exp`. The `exp` term is unwanted.

Candidate 46: `P**2*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(P*c3) + c4*log(P*c5 + 1) + c6*cos(...)`
Has `log`, `cos`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 47: `(P*c0 + (P + c1)*(P*c2 + 1)*(P*c3 + c4*(P*c2 + 1)*exp(P*c5) + c6 + c7*cos(...)))/(P + c1)`
Has `cos`. NO MATCH.

Candidate 48: `(P*c0 + (P*c1 + 1)*(P*c2 + c3*(P + 1)*exp(P*c4) + (P*c1 + 1)*(P*c5 + c6)))/(P + c7)`
Denominator `P+c7`. Numerator has `P*c1+1`. If `c1=1/c7`, `P/c7+1 = (P+c7)/c7`.
Then `(P*c1+1)/(P+c7) = 1/c7`.
Expression = `P*c0/(P+c7) + (1/c7)*(P*c2 + c3(P+1)exp + (P*c1+1)(P*c5+c6))`.
Rational term `P*c0/(P+c7)` unless `c0=0`.
If `c0=0`, we have `(1/c7)[ c2 P + c3(P+1)exp + (P/c7+1)(c5 P + c6) ]`.
= `(c2/c7) P + (c3/c7)(P+1)exp + (1/c7)(P/c7+1)(c5 P + c6)`.
`(P+1)exp` gives `exp` term. Unwanted.
So NO MATCH.

Candidate 49: `(P*c0 + (P*c1 + 1)*(P + c2*(P*c1 + 1)*exp(P*c3) + (P*c1 + 1)*(P*c4 + c5)))/(P + c6)`
Denominator `P+c6`. Numerator `P*c1+1`. If `c1=1/c6`, cancels.
Expression = `P*c0/(P+c6) + (1/c6)*(P + c2(P/c6+1)exp + (P/c6+1)(P*c4+c5))`.
Rational term `P*c0/(P+c6)` unless `c0=0`.
If `c0=0`, `(1/c6)P + (c2/c6)(P/c6+1)exp + (1/c6)(P/c6+1)(P*c4+c5)`.
`(P/c6+1)exp` gives `exp` term. Unwanted.
So NO MATCH.

Candidate 50: `(P*c0*(P + c1) + (P*c2 + 1)*(P*c3 + (P + c1)*(P*c4 + 1)*(P*c5 + c6*(P*c4 + 1)*exp(P*c7) + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c8 + c9))))/((P + c1)*(P*c2 + 1))`
Denominator `(P+c1)(P*c2+1)`.
Numerator: `P*c0*(P+c1)` divisible by `P+c1`.
Second part: `(P*c2+1)*(...)` divisible by `P*c2+1`.
Simplifies to `P*c0 + P*c3 + (P+c1)*(P*c4+1)*(P*c5 + c6(P*c4+1)exp + (P*c4+1)(P*c8+c9))`.
This has `(P+c1)(P*c4+1) = P^2 c4 + P(c1 c4 + 1) + c1`.
Multiplied by `(P*c5 + ...)`. This will produce `P^3` terms unless coefficients are zero.
GT is degree 2 polynomial + `P exp`. This candidate easily produces higher degrees.
To match GT, we need to kill `P^3`, `P^2 exp`, etc.
Set `c6=0` to remove `exp` part? But we need `exp`.
If `c6 != 0`, we have `(P+c1)(P*c4+1)^2 exp`. This is `P^2 exp` etc. Unwanted.
So `c6` must be 0, but then no `exp`.
So NO MATCH.

Basis: `P^2`, `P`, `P exp(k P)`.
All candidates 11, 12, 13, 14, 15, 16, 18, 19, 20 match this basis exactly.

What about Candidate 1? `(P*c0*(P + c1)*exp(P*c2) + P*c3 + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c5 + c6*(P*c4 + 1)*exp(P*c7) + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c8 + c9)))/(P + c1)`
If we set `c4 = 1/c1`, then `P*c4+1 = (P+c1)/c1`.
Numerator becomes `P*c0*(P+c1)exp(P*c2) + P*c3 + ((P+c1)/c1)*(P*c5 + c6*((P+c1)/c1)*exp(P*c7) + ((P+c1)/c1)*(P*c8+c9))`
Divide by `P+c1`:
= `P*c0*exp(P*c2) + P*c3/(P+c1) + (1/c1)*P*c5 + (c6/c1^2)*(P+c1)*exp(P*c7) + (1/c1^2)*(P+c1)*(P*c8+c9)`
This has `P/(P+c1)` term. Unless `c3=0`.
If `c3=0`, we have `P*c0*exp(P*c2) + (c5/c1)P + (c6/c1^2)(P+c1)exp(P*c7) + (1/c1^2)(P^2 c8 + P c9 + P c1 c8 + c1 c9)`.
= `P*c0*exp(P*c2) + (c5/c1)P + (c6/c1^2)P exp(P*c7) + (c6/c1)exp(P*c7) + (c8/c1^2)P^2 + (c9/c1^2 + c8/c1)P + c9/c1`.
This has a constant term `c9/c1` and a standalone `exp` term `(c6/c1)exp(P*c7)`.
GT has no constant and no standalone `exp`.
We can set `c9=0` to remove constant.
We can set `c6=0` to remove standalone `exp`, but then we lose the `P exp` term from that part. We still have `P*c0*exp(P*c2)`.
So if `c6=0, c9=0, c3=0`, we get:
`P*c0*exp(P*c2) + (c5/c1)P + (c8/c1^2)P^2 + (c8/c1)P`
= `(c8/c1^2)P^2 + (c5/c1 + c8/c1)P + c0 P exp(P*c2)`.
This matches the form `A P^2 + B P + C P exp(D P)`!
So Candidate 1 CAN match by setting specific constants. The prompt says "Candidate constants are FREE. You can assign ANY real number...". So if it can be made equivalent, it's a MATCH.
However, usually in these benchmarks, they expect direct structural matches or simple ones. But mathematically, Candidate 1 is a MATCH.
Let's check Candidate 2: `P*(c0 + c1*(P*c2 + c3*(P*c1 + 1)*exp(P*c4) + (P*c1 + 1)*(P*c5 + c6)))/(P + c7)`
Denominator `P+c7`. Numerator has `P*c1+1`. If `c1=1/c7`, `P/c7+1 = (P+c7)/c7`.
Expression = `P*(c0 + c1*(P*c2 + c3*((P+c7)/c7)*exp + ((P+c7)/c7)*(P*c5+c6)))/(P+c7)`
= `P*c0/(P+c7) + P*c1*c2/(P+c7) + P*c1*c3/c7 * exp + P*c1/c7 * (P*c5+c6)`.
Rational terms `P/(P+c7)` unless `c0=0, c2=0`.
If `c0=0, c2=0`, we get `P*c1*c3/c7 exp(P*c4) + P*c1/c7 (c5 P + c6)`
= `(c1 c3 / c7) P exp(P*c4) + (c1 c5 / c7) P^2 + (c1 c6 / c7) P`.
Matches form! So Candidate 2 is a MATCH.

Candidate 3: `P*(P*c0 + 1)*(c1*exp(P*c2) + c3 + c4*(P*c0 + 1))/(P + c5)`
Denominator `P+c5`. Numerator has `P*c0+1`. If `c0=1/c5`, `P/c5+1 = (P+c5)/c5`.
Expression = `P*((P+c5)/c5)*(c1 exp + c3 + c4*(P+c5)/c5)/(P+c5)`
= `P/c5 * (c1 exp + c3 + c4/c5 (P+c5))`
= `(c1/c5) P exp + (c3/c5) P + (c4/c5^2) P(P+c5)`
= `(c1/c5) P exp + (c3/c5) P + (c4/c5^2) P^2 + (c4/c5) P`
= `(c4/c5^2) P^2 + (c3/c5 + c4/c5) P + (c1/c5) P exp`.
Matches form! So Candidate 3 is a MATCH.

Candidate 4: `P*(P*c0 + c1*(P*c2 + 1)*exp(P*c3) + c4 + (P*c2 + 1)*(P*c5 + c6))/(P*c2 + 1)`
Denominator `P*c2+1`. Numerator has `P*c2+1` in two terms.
First term `P*c0` and `c4` are not divisible by `P*c2+1` unless `c0=0, c4=0`.
If `c0=0, c4=0`, expression = `P*( c1(P*c2+1)exp + (P*c2+1)(P*c5+c6) ) / (P*c2+1)`
= `P*( c1 exp + P*c5 + c6 )`
= `c1 P exp + c5 P^2 + c6 P`.
Matches form! So Candidate 4 is a MATCH.

Candidate 5: `P*c0 + c1*exp(P*c2) + (P + 1)*(P*c3 + P + c4*exp(P*c5))`
= `c0 P + c1 exp + c3 P^2 + c3 P + P^2 + P + c4 P exp + c4 exp`
= `(c3+1) P^2 + (c0+c3+1) P + (c1+c4) exp + c4 P exp`.
Has standalone `exp` term `(c1+c4) exp`. GT has none.
Can we set `c1 = -c4`? Yes.
Then `exp` term vanishes.
Result: `(c3+1) P^2 + (c0+c3+1) P + c4 P exp`.
Matches form! So Candidate 5 is a MATCH.

Candidate 6: `P*c0*(P*c1 + 1) + c2*exp(P*c3) + (P + 1)*(P*c4 + P + c5*exp(P*c6))`
= `c0 c1 P^2 + c0 P + c2 exp + c4 P^2 + c4 P + P^2 + P + c5 P exp + c5 exp`
= `(c0 c1 + c4 + 1) P^2 + (c0 + c4 + 1) P + (c2 + c5) exp + c5 P exp`.
Set `c2 = -c5` to kill standalone `exp`.
Matches form! So Candidate 6 is a MATCH.

Candidate 7: `P*c0*exp(P*c1) + c2 + (P*c3 + 1)*(P*c4 + c5*(P*c3 + 1))`
= `c0 P exp + c2 + c4 P(P*c3+1) + c5(P*c3+1)^2`
= `c0 P exp + c2 + c4 c3 P^2 + c4 P + c5(c3^2 P^2 + 2 c3 P + 1)`
= `(c4 c3 + c5 c3^2) P^2 + (c4 + 2 c5 c3) P + (c2 + c5) + c0 P exp`.
Has constant `c2+c5`. Set `c2 = -c5`.
Matches form! So Candidate 7 is a MATCH.

Candidate 8: `P*c0*exp(P*c1) + P*c2 + c3 + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c5 + c6*(P*c4 + 1))`
= `c0 P exp + c2 P + c3 + c5 P(P*c4+1) + c6(P*c4+1)^2`
= `c0 P exp + c2 P + c3 + c5 c4 P^2 + c5 P + c6(c4^2 P^2 + 2 c4 P + 1)`
= `(c5 c4 + c6 c4^2) P^2 + (c2 + c5 + 2 c6 c4) P + (c3 + c6) + c0 P exp`.
Set `c3 = -c6` to kill constant.
Matches form! So Candidate 8 is a MATCH.

Candidate 9: `P*c0*exp(P*c1) + c2 + (P + 1)*(P*c3 + P + c4)`
= `c0 P exp + c2 + c3 P^2 + c3 P + P^2 + P + c4 P + c4`
= `(c3+1) P^2 + (c3+1+c4) P + (c2+c4) + c0 P exp`.
Set `c2 = -c4` to kill constant.
Matches form! So Candidate 9 is a MATCH.

Candidate 10: `P*c0*exp(P*c1) + (P*c2 + 1)*(P*c3 + c4*(P*c2 + 1) + c5*(P*c2 + 1))`

It seems almost all candidates from 1 to 20 can be tuned to match the form `A P^2 + B P + C P exp(D P)`.
Let's verify this pattern. The GT is essentially a quadratic polynomial in P plus a P*exp term.
Many candidates are constructed as sums of polynomials and exponentials, possibly with rational parts that cancel out, or extra terms that can be zeroed out.
Given the instruction "Candidate constants are FREE. You can assign ANY real number... to candidate constants or freely modify explicit numbers", if a candidate can be algebraically reduced to the target form by setting constants, it is a MATCH.
I will mark 1 through 20 as MATCH, except 17 which has `Max(0, P-1)` (piecewise, not smooth polynomial/exp).
Wait, let's check 17 again: `P*(c0 + c1*exp(P*c2) + c3*Max(0, P - 1))`.
`Max(0, P-1)` is `0` for `P<1` and `P-1` for `P>=1`.
GT is smooth everywhere. `Max` introduces a kink at `P=1`. So 17 is NO MATCH.

What about 21-50? I already checked many and found they have `log`, `cos`, or irreducible rational parts, or higher degree terms that can't be killed without killing the `exp` term.
Let's quickly re-verify 21: `(P*c0 + c1*(P + c2)*exp(P*c3) + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c5 + c6*(P*c4 + 1)*exp(P*c7) + (P*c4 + 1)*(P*c8 + c9)))/(P + c2)`
If `c4 = 1/c2`, `P*c4+1 = (P+c2)/c2`.
Expression = `P*c0/(P+c2) + c1 exp + (1/c2)*(P*c5 + c6((P+c2)/c2)exp + ((P+c2)/c2)(P*c8+c9))`
= `P*c0/(P+c2) + c1 exp + (c5/c2)P + (c6/c2^2)(P+c2)exp + (1/c2^2)(P+c2)(P*c8+c9)`

= `(c8/c2^2) P^2 + (c5/c2 + c9/c2^2 + c8/c2) P + (c1 + c6/c2) exp + (c6/c2^2) P exp + c9/c2`.

Then we get `(c8/c2^2) P^2 + (c5/c2 + c8/c2) P + (c6/c2^2) P exp`.
Matches form! So 21 is MATCH.

This implies many candidates are MATCH. The prompt says "verify which candidates mathematically equate to the Ground Truth". Given the flexibility of constants, almost all polynomial+exp combinations that can be reduced to `A P^2 + B P + C P exp(D P)` are matches.

Let's check 22-50 again. They mostly contain `log` or `cos`. `log` and `cos` are linearly independent from polynomials and `exp`. They cannot be zeroed out unless their coefficients are 0. If coefficients are 0, they vanish. But do they have enough free parameters to match the target while zeroing out `log`/`cos`?
Candidate 22: `c0*log(P*c1 + 1) + (P*c2 + 1)*(P*c3 + c4*(P*c2 + 1)*exp(P*c5) + (P*c2 + 1)*(P*c6 + c7*cos(c8*exp(P*c9))))`
Set `c0=0`, `c7=0`.
= `(P*c2+1)(P*c3 + c4(P*c2+1)exp(P*c5) + (P*c2+1)P*c6)`
= `c3 P(P*c2+1) + c4(P*c2+1)^2 exp + c6 P(P*c2+1)^2`
= `c3 c2 P^2 + c3 P + c4(c2^2 P^2 + 2 c2 P + 1) exp + c6 P(c2^2 P^2 + 2 c2 P + 1)`
This has `P^3` term from `c6 P^3 c2^2`. Set `c6=0`.
Then `c3 c2 P^2 + c3 P + c4(c2^2 P^2 + 2 c2 P + 1) exp`.
Has standalone `exp` term `c4 exp`. Set `c4=0`? Then no `exp`.
We need `P exp`. The `exp` term here is `(P*c2+1)^2 exp = (c2^2 P^2 + 2 c2 P + 1) exp`.
To get only `P exp`, we need `c2=0`. If `c2=0`, `(P*c2+1)=1`.
Then expression = `c3 P + c4 exp + c6 P`.
No `P^2` term. So cannot match GT.
Thus 22 is NO MATCH.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`GT = c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P`
Expanding and grouping by basis functions:
`GT = (c0*c1 + c3*c4)*P - (c0/c2)*P^2 - c3*P*exp(-c5*P)`
This is a linear combination of three basis functions: `P^2`, `P`, and `P*exp(k*P)`. Any candidate that can be algebraically reduced to the form `A*P^2 + B*P + C*P*exp(D*P)` by assigning appropriate values to its free constants is a `[MATCH]`. Candidates containing irreducible rational terms, standalone `exp`/`log`/`cos` terms that cannot be zeroed out without destroying the target structure, or piecewise functions like `Max` are `[NO MATCH]`.

### Candidate Analysis
**Candidate 1:** Expands to rational form. Setting `c4=1/c1` cancels the denominator. Setting `c3=0, c6=0, c9=0` removes rational/constant/standalone-exp terms. Reduces to `A*P^2 + B*P + C*P*exp(D*P)`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 2:** Denominator `P+c7` cancels if `c1=1/c7`. Setting `c0=0, c2=0` removes rational terms. Reduces to `A*P^2 + B*P + C*P*exp(D*P)`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 3:** Denominator `P+c5` cancels if `c0=1/c5`. Expands directly to `A*P^2 + B*P + C*P*exp(D*P)`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 4:** Denominator `P*c2+1` cancels terms in numerator. Setting `c0=0, c4=0` removes non-divisible parts. Reduces to `A*P^2 + B*P + C*P*exp(D*P)`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 5:** Expands to `(c3+1)P^2 + (c0+c3+1)P + (c1+c4)exp + c4*P*exp`. Setting `c1=-c4` kills standalone `exp`. Matches target basis. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 6:** Expands to `(c0*c1+c4+1)P^2 + (c0+c4+1)P + (c2+c5)exp + c5*P*exp`. Setting `c2=-c5` kills standalone `exp`. Matches target basis. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 7:** Expands to `(c4*c3+c5*c3^2)P^2 + (c4+2*c5*c3)P + (c2+c5) + c0*P*exp`. Setting `c2=-c5` kills constant. Matches target basis. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 8:** Expands to `(c5*c4+c6*c4^2)P^2 + (c2+c5+2*c6*c4)P + (c3+c6) + c0*P*exp`. Setting `c3=-c6` kills constant. Matches target basis. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 9:** Expands to `(c3+1)P^2 + (c3+1+c4)P + (c2+c4) + c0*P*exp`. Setting `c2=-c4` kills constant. Matches target basis. `[MATCH]`

**Candidate 11:** `P*(P*c0 + P + c1*exp(P*c2) + c3) = (c0+1)P^2 + c3*P + c1*P*exp(P*c2)`. Direct match. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 12:** `P*(P*c0 + c1*(P*c2 + 1) + c3*exp(P*c4) + c5) = (c0+c1*c2)P^2 + (c1+c5)P + c3*P*exp(P*c4)`. Direct match. `[MATCH]`

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

**GT expression:**
$$f(P) = 0.5980\cdot(1 - P/32.939)\cdot P + 0.5980\cdot(1 - e^{-0.0768P})\cdot P$$

Expanding:
$$f(P) = 0.5980P - 0.5980P^2/32.939 + 0.5980P - 0.5980P\cdot e^{-0.0768P}$$
$$= 1.1961P - 0.01815P^2 - 0.5980P\cdot e^{-0.0768P}$$

So the GT has the form: **aP² + bP + cP·exp(dP)** where d < 0.

This means the GT is: `α·P² + β·P + γ·P·exp(δ·P)` with specific constants.

Let me check candidates that have this structure.

**Candidate 11:** `P*(P*c0 + P + c1*exp(P*c2) + c3)` = `P²*c0 + P² + P*c1*exp(P*c2) + P*c3`
This has P² terms and P·exp(P·c2) and P terms. But there's a fixed coefficient of 1 on P². Wait - the "P" term inside gives P², but we can't zero it out since it has no constant. Actually, this is `(c0+1)P² + c1·P·exp(c2·P) + c3·P`. Setting c0+1 = -0.01815, c3 = 1.1961, c1 = -0.5980, c2 = -0.0768. This works! The "+P" inside gives a fixed P² term, but c0 can compensate. Yes, this matches.

**Candidate 12:** `P*(P*c0 + c1*(P*c2 + 1) + c3*exp(P*c4) + c5)` = `P*(P*c0 + c1*c2*P + c1 + c3*exp(P*c4) + c5)` = `P²(c0 + c1*c2) + P(c1 + c5) + P*c3*exp(P*c4)`. This has the right structure: aP² + bP + cP·exp(dP). ✓

**Candidate 13:** `P*(c0*(P*c1 + 1) + c2 + c3*exp(P*c4))` = `P*(c0*c1*P + c0 + c2 + c3*exp(P*c4))` = `c0*c1*P² + (c0+c2)*P + c3*P*exp(c4*P)`. Same structure. ✓

**Candidate 14:** `P*(P*c0 + P*c1 + c2*exp(P*c3) + c4)` = `(c0+c1)P² + c4*P + c2*P*exp(c3*P)`. Same structure. ✓

**Candidate 15:** `P*(c0 + c1*exp(P*c2) + c3*Abs(P))` With P ≥ 0: `c3*P² + c0*P + c1*P*exp(c2*P)`. ✓

**Candidate 16:** `P*(c0 + c1*exp(P*c2)) + c3*Abs(P)**2` With P ≥ 0: `c3*P² + c0*P + c1*P*exp(c2*P)`. ✓

**Candidate 18:** `P*(c0*exp(P*c1) + c2*(P*c3 + 1))` = `c2*c3*P² + c2*P + c0*P*exp(c1*P)`. ✓

**Candidate 19:** With P ≥ 0: same as `P*(P*c0 + c1*exp(c2*P) + c3)` = `c0*P² + c3*P + c1*P*exp(c2*P)`. ✓
